## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models population growth rate dP/dt as a function of population P and time t, which is the fundamental problem in population dynamics. Classical models range from simple exponential growth to density-dependent and time-varying models.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Malthusian growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (exponential growth, density-independent)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Strong Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population)
- Weak Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 + P) (depensation without extinction threshold)
- Beverton-Holt type: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (rational density dependence with mortality)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional power scaling of growth rate)
- Von Bertalanffy type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance)
- Time-varying logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (seasonal carrying capacity)
- Time-dependent rate: dP_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * P (exponentially changing growth rate)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * c3 (generalized asymmetric growth)
- Polynomial density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (higher-order density effects)
- Logistic with harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (constant yield harvesting)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope тЖТ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects тЖТ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay тЖТ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior тЖТ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects тЖТ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Quadratic dependence on P (P - P┬▓ pattern) тЖТ logistic-type density-dependent regulation with carrying capacity
- Cubic dependence on P (P┬▓ - P┬│ or P┬╖(P-a)┬╖(1-P/K)) тЖТ Allee effect with critical population threshold
- Logarithmic coupling log(P) multiplied by P тЖТ Gompertz-type asymmetric growth near carrying capacity
- Rational dependence P/(1+P) тЖТ contest competition or resource saturation in population interactions
- Periodic time modulation sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) multiplying growth terms тЖТ seasonal or cyclic environmental forcing
- Difference of power laws P^a - P^b тЖТ metabolic scaling models balancing anabolic and catabolic processes
- Growth rate vanishing at two positive P values тЖТ bistability or Allee effect dynamics
- Linear dP/dt vs P relationship тЖТ Malthusian regime; curvature indicates density regulation onset
- Exponential decay in time multiplying P-dependent terms тЖТ transient environmental change or resource depletion
- Product of multiple linear factors in P тЖТ multiple equilibria in population dynamics (stable and unstable fixed points)

$$GT = 0.201P(-1 + P/5.637)(1 - P/10.233) + 0.201P + \frac{0.201P}{1 + e^{-5.637(-0.634 + P)}}$$

Let me expand the polynomial part:
- $0.201P(-1 + P/5.637)(1 - P/10.233)$
- $= 0.201P \cdot \frac{(P - 5.637)(10.233 - P)}{5.637 \times 10.233}$
- $= 0.201P \cdot \frac{-P^2 + 15.87P - 57.683}{57.683}$

This gives: $0.201 \cdot (-P^3/57.683 + 15.87P^2/57.683 - P) + 0.201P$

So the polynomial part is: $aP^3 + bP^2 + cP$ where $a < 0, b > 0$.

The sigmoid part is: $\frac{0.201P}{1 + e^{-5.637(P - 0.634)}}$

This is a sigmoidal function of P multiplied by P. The GT depends only on P (not t), since t doesn't appear.

**Key observation**: The GT has no dependence on t. So any candidate with t-dependent terms that can't be zeroed out won't work.

For candidates with t terms that have free coefficients (like c5*t/...), those coefficients can be set to 0. But terms like `t/(P+c6)**5` (with coefficient 1, not a free constant) cannot be zeroed.

Now, the GT has a sigmoid-like term. Among the candidates, I need one that can produce:
1. A cubic polynomial in P: $P^3 c_0 + P^2 c_1 + P c_2$ тЬУ (most have this)
2. A sigmoid-like term: $\frac{cP}{1 + e^{-a(P-b)}}$

Looking at candidates with `exp(P*c)` terms:
- **Candidate 1**: Has `c5*exp(P*c6)` - this is just an exponential, not a sigmoid.
- **Candidate 32, 36, 37**: Have `c3*exp(P*c4)` - plain exponential, not sigmoid form.

The sigmoid $\frac{P}{1+e^{-a(P-b)}}$ cannot be expressed as a sum of simple functions like polynomials, exponentials, powers, logs, sines, or rational functions of the form $1/(P+c)^n$.

None of the candidates contain a sigmoid or logistic-type function. The GT's sigmoid term $\frac{0.201P}{1+e^{-5.637(P-0.634)}}$ transitions smoothly from ~0 (for small P) to ~0.201P (for large P). This behavior cannot be replicated by:
- Power terms $P^c$ (these are smooth power laws)
- Exponential terms $e^{cP}$ (these grow/decay monotonically without saturation)
- Rational terms $1/(P+c)^n$ (these decay as powers)
- Log terms $\log(cP+1)$
- Sin terms

WaitтАФcould $P^{c_3} \cdot c_4$ somehow replicate a sigmoid times P? No, $P^{c_3}$ is a single power law.

Could `c3*exp(P*c4) + c5/(P+c6)^n` somehow combine to form a sigmoid? The sigmoid is $\frac{1}{1+e^{-x}} = \frac{e^x}{1+e^x}$, which is not expressible as a sum of an exponential and rational terms.

None of the candidate formulas contain the structural elements needed to reproduce the logistic/sigmoid function present in the GT. The sigmoid function $\frac{P}{1+e^{f(P)}}$ requires a ratio involving an exponential in the denominator, which none of the candidates provide.

## GT Analysis

The GT is:
```
0.201*(-1 + P/5.637)*(1 - P/10.233)*P + 0.201*P + 0.201*P/(1 + exp(-5.637*(-0.634 + P)))
```

Let me expand this:
- First term: `0.201*(-1 + P/5.637)*(1 - P/10.233)*P` тАФ this is a cubic polynomial in P
- Second term: `0.201*P` тАФ linear in P
- Third term: `0.201*P/(1 + exp(-5.637*(-0.634 + P)))` тАФ this is P times a sigmoid function

Let me expand the cubic part:
(-1 + P/5.637)(1 - P/10.233) = -1 + P/10.233 + P/5.637 - P┬▓/(5.637├Ч10.233)

So the first term = 0.201*P*[-1 + P/10.233 + P/5.637 - P┬▓/57.683]

= 0.201*[-P + P┬▓/10.233 + P┬▓/5.637 - P┬│/57.683]

Combined with 0.201*P: the -P and +P cancel, leaving:
= 0.201*[P┬▓/10.233 + P┬▓/5.637 - P┬│/57.683] + sigmoid term

= 0.201*P┬▓*(1/10.233 + 1/5.637) - 0.201*P┬│/57.683 + 0.201*P/(1 + exp(-5.637*(P - 0.634)))

The GT has these basis functions:
1. **P┬│** (polynomial)
2. **P┬▓** (polynomial)
3. **P/(1 + exp(aP + b))** тАФ a sigmoid-weighted P term

This is crucial: the GT contains a **sigmoid function** of P. This is `P/(1 + exp(-5.637*(P - 0.634)))`.

Now I need to check which candidates can reproduce a sigmoid function.

## Candidate Analysis

The sigmoid `P/(1+exp(c*(P-d)))` cannot be expressed as:
- Polynomials in P
- Power functions P^c
- Rational functions like 1/(P+c)^n
- sin, cos, log functions
- exp(cP) alone (without the denominator structure)

Let me check each candidate for the presence of a sigmoid-like term:

**Candidates with `t` dependence** (2, 4, 6, 8, 11, 12, 13, 15, 16, 17, 18, 19, 20, 21, 24, 27, 29, 30, 31, 35, 38, 39, 40, 41, 42, 43, 48, 49): These have terms involving `t`. Since GT has no `t` dependence, the `t`-dependent terms must be zeroed out. After zeroing, we need to check if the remaining terms can match GT. But zeroing `t` terms removes potential sigmoid approximations.

For candidates without `t`:
- **Candidates with exp(P*c)**: 1, 32, 36, 37 тАФ `exp(cP)` alone is NOT the same as `P/(1+exp(cP))`. These are fundamentally different basis functions.
- **Candidates with sin**: 22, 50 тАФ sin cannot match sigmoid
- **Candidates with log**: 23, 44, 47 тАФ log cannot match sigmoid
- **Candidates with P^c**: 1, 5, 9, 10, 45 тАФ P^c is a power law, not sigmoid
- **Candidates with only rational/polynomial**: 3, 7, 25, 26, 28, 33, 34, 46 тАФ cannot match sigmoid

None of these basis functions can exactly reproduce `P/(1 + exp(c*(P-d)))` for all P. The sigmoid is a fundamentally different function that cannot be expressed as any finite combination of polynomials, power laws, rational functions, exponentials, logarithms, or trigonometric functions.

After careful analysis, **no candidate** contains the sigmoid structure `P/(1 + exp(...))` needed to match the GT.

Let me verify candidates 1-50 systematically тАФ none have the form `P/(1+exp(...))` or equivalent.

Candidate 1 through 50 verdict: [NO MATCH] for all.

Matched candidate IDs: []

[NO MATCH]

Conclusion: No match
